  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d27e00c1-0b2e-4c8e-bf57-a0042205d3e9'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer18327706731730409089">Mello and Matt are the highlights of this series! I need more of them... They need their own series! They are my favourite team. And I fear to say that if it came to Mello/Matt vs Kira, I would be supporting Mello and Matt!<br/><br/>Loved Misa in this one, she's hilarious and I loved Mello's reaction to her, so much fun. <br/><br/>However, I have to say that I miss the old days where Light could freely communicate with Ryuk. Now, we have Ryuk on the page but he's just there, standing and watching. The apple loving </span>
  <span id="freeText18327706731730409089" style="display:none">Mello and Matt are the highlights of this series! I need more of them... They need their own series! They are my favourite team. And I fear to say that if it came to Mello/Matt vs Kira, I would be supporting Mello and Matt!<br /><br />Loved Misa in this one, she's hilarious and I loved Mello's reaction to her, so much fun. <br /><br />However, I have to say that I miss the old days where Light could freely communicate with Ryuk. Now, we have Ryuk on the page but he's just there, standing and watching. The apple loving creature needs more space! And I want Mello to meet Ryuk!<br /><br />And hopefully, I don't even need to mention that I don't like Near. The monkey child is rather boring and honestly, he does not seem to have any ideas of his own. L thought that something was true so Near follows it. <br /></span>

<div id="review_662897532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/662897532" />
    <a title="Allan Hunt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21085350-allan-hunt"><img alt="Allan Hunt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370570642p2/21085350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/662897532?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allan Hunt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allan Hunt" href="/user/show/21085350-allan-hunt">Allan Hunt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662897532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14884932104130799856">Since Volume 7 or 8, my fondness for this series has started to flag, and the reasons why were particularly evident in this volume: a cast of unlikable characters, tortured storylines and lack of thought. Spoilers ahead.<br/><br/>Even though the characters were either ineffectual (Matsuda, Sochiro Yagami), evil (Light, L arguably, Mello) or kind of silly (Miss), you could always see where they were coming from and relate. Insights were clearly explained and understandable, motives clear. You were impresse</span>
  <span id="freeText14884932104130799856" style="display:none">Since Volume 7 or 8, my fondness for this series has started to flag, and the reasons why were particularly evident in this volume: a cast of unlikable characters, tortured storylines and lack of thought. Spoilers ahead.<br /><br />Even though the characters were either ineffectual (Matsuda, Sochiro Yagami), evil (Light, L arguably, Mello) or kind of silly (Miss), you could always see where they were coming from and relate. Insights were clearly explained and understandable, motives clear. You were impressed with L'a conclusions and Lights countermeasures were logical if somewhat unrealistic (but within the realms of acceptable suspension of disbelief). You couldn't help but like Matsuda and Mogi's attempts to contribute, even though they were well out of their league. Even Mello's efforts were logical, if brutal. Unfortunately, all that has ended.<br /><br />Nears conclusion that Light is Kira has yet to be even remotely logically supported by a shred of evidence. At best he proves that it *could* be the case, that it isn't impossible. This would be a fine start, except he goes on to dismantle the efforts of Light and his team to find Kira: fine if he's right, but catastrophic if he's wrong. It's impossible to respect his alleged intellect, when all he does is respout L's conclusions and evidence of doubtful veracity provided by Mello, who has a clear motive to lead Near in the wrong direction, and who should be treated as morally unacceptable as Kira himself. The attempt to go in a different direction to L is commendable, but in this case it hasn't worked out, and relies heavily on plot-forcing, rather than logical progression. The suspicion stirred up in people who should have been the last people to suspect Light was dine entirely too easily, given what we know of the characters involved, and no justification given.<br /><br />All in all, it comes off as extremely forced: Tsugumi Ohba set up a fantastic story and set of characters, but now has been forcing the story to end with the "bad guy" defeated and the "good guys" victorious, regardless of whether it actually makes sense or not. A real decline of a story I deeply, deeply enjoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14884932104130799856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2496973898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2496973898" />
    <a title="Makrand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80273455-makrand"><img alt="Makrand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594039173p2/80273455.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14384073931431049930">With only two volumes left to the series it is probable that the creators knew I would keep reading no matter how dull and drawn out the conversations had become in this series. Unless they knew I found the conversations dull. Then they were intending to bore me, but threw in Mikami to completely take me by surprise. Unless I read it on a Saturday. Then it would be obvious that the bagel I ate was far more interesting to read than a new origin story about a magical killing person. But they antic</span>
  <span id="freeText14384073931431049930" style="display:none">With only two volumes left to the series it is probable that the creators knew I would keep reading no matter how dull and drawn out the conversations had become in this series. Unless they knew I found the conversations dull. Then they were intending to bore me, but threw in Mikami to completely take me by surprise. Unless I read it on a Saturday. Then it would be obvious that the bagel I ate was far more interesting to read than a new origin story about a magical killing person. But they anticipated that I would find that plot line tedious so they tossed in some Mika scenes and the new eyecandy chic to distract me from the novelesque word balloons and chore-like storyline. The creators have out-thought me at every step of the way. Truly brilliant. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14384073931431049930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8430275792656431674" style="display:none">The cover of this one is so badass. Probably my favourite of the lot.<br /><br />It looks like everything is beginning to unravel now...<br /><br />This is when <i>Death Note</i> is at its mind boggling best - when the characters are all second guessing each other, putting up fronts, vying for the upper hand... Oooh, it's good. Kinda crazy to follow at times.<br /><br />Light is becoming so evil and manipulative... He acknowledges Misa's vulnerability and lack of self-worth, but continues to use her without a second thought. He allows her to literally destroy her life, as long as he gets what he wants.<br /><br />He has no respect for anyone or the sanctity of life anymore - he decides to build a relationship with Takada just so he can <i>'control her however he wants'.</i> Dude.<br /><br />Well, except his own, what with him being a god incarnate an' all. Why should anyone else's puny life get in the way of his divine vision, huh?<br /><br />And yet he still has that irresistible charm. He's undeniably a fascinating character, a proper love-to-hate guy.<br /><br />Onwards to the penultimate volume!<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156559583" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156559583?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eyla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eyla" href="/user/show/59876764-eyla">Eyla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156559583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6371602731664704036">Okay, wow. This volume took me a while to get through, it is very dialogue heavy. I mean, in this series, it's nothing new, it just took me a lot longer to get through than I thought it would.<br/>To start, I just want to say how much I hate the way Light thinks of women. And, to be honest, the way the women are represented in this series in general isn't great at all. As a woman myself, I hate seeing so many similar female characters and how poor their thinking processes and personalities are. I do </span>
  <span id="freeText6371602731664704036" style="display:none">Okay, wow. This volume took me a while to get through, it is very dialogue heavy. I mean, in this series, it's nothing new, it just took me a lot longer to get through than I thought it would.<br />To start, I just want to say how much I hate the way Light thinks of women. And, to be honest, the way the women are represented in this series in general isn't great at all. As a woman myself, I hate seeing so many similar female characters and how poor their thinking processes and personalities are. I do understand that some of the traits portrayed in these women are found in a lot of girls around the world but in no cases have I ever found women who are so desperate for a man to love them that they quite their passion just to satisfy them. The scene in the previous volume with Misa and Light had me annoyed to the point of gritting my teeth. But then he plays with another woman's emotions just to get what he wants. I loved Penbar's fiance (or was it his wife?) from the first few volumes of the series, and even the chick in the SPK is cool. But characters like Misa have me wishing to tear my hair out.<br /><br />If you made it all the way here, thank you for putting up with my rant. Of course, plot is still going strong in this volume and the author continues to find ways to keep the story fresh enough to have the readers keep reading. Overall, I think I like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6371602731664704036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3029125909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029125909" />
    <a title="Jpage20" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102370130-jpage20"><img alt="Jpage20" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029125909?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jpage20" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jpage20" href="/user/show/102370130-jpage20">Jpage20</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3029125909&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029125909" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17818670756223443581">Another volume of Death Note that just reels you in, the story starts to accelerate even faster. The name of this volume is named "Deletion" because of the person Kira chooses to become the next holder of the Death Note. Mikami, a devoted Kira worshipper often says the phrase "Delete" when he viciously writes down the names he's ordered to kill. The art style in this volume is no different than the other books of this series, but that isn't a bad thing at all because I really enjoyed the same st</span>
  <span id="freeText17818670756223443581" style="display:none">Another volume of Death Note that just reels you in, the story starts to accelerate even faster. The name of this volume is named "Deletion" because of the person Kira chooses to become the next holder of the Death Note. Mikami, a devoted Kira worshipper often says the phrase "Delete" when he viciously writes down the names he's ordered to kill. The art style in this volume is no different than the other books of this series, but that isn't a bad thing at all because I really enjoyed the same style instead of them changing it midway through. With the introduction of the two new Kira connections, I thought they were somewhat good characters, more Mikami than the female broadcaster whose name I forgot. An overall analysis of Mikami shows that he was a normal person living a diligent scheduled life, even after he was chosen to become Kira's right hand man. He had a short development spotlight, and his backstory was shown as to why he was the way he was now.<br /><br />I would recommend this book, well because it is still the most popular anime, and the manga is honestly better in my opinion. Not a big fan of reading things that take a lot of time, but the 7 volumes I read for a project went by so quickly that I want to rewatch the anime as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17818670756223443581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w4pP5mXVR1tJjZNmyiG/u9q6UuH+q7BaTQiZI8f5NgzT2t/W2Yk7M2RdsU3ioBQjwY/C7CnksqR113z7/xZcjw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6nGBGJYzXXSO0oR4FwiVwMRlXEWm7nwIvUDTyuGlP236IREoKm8hHKMCplM/iT5Y31DMSHGhfvaFnzYS2UpV7g==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5038071399668838801">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText5038071399668838801" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
